I interpret "The Only Heartbreaker" as a toxic relationship where Mitski's partner is constantly blaming her for everything going wrong in their relationship. The partner delusionally sees themself as the blameless one when in reality they are both to blame. I interpret this song with a sense of sarcasm from Mitski, who also, amidst this toxic relationship, begins to believe the lies her partner has been telling her which makes it all the more confusing, not knowing whether to trust herself or her partner's lies.

I don't really see this as a song about self sabotage but a person who is in an unhealthy relationship.  It's a relationship where their partner finds faults in everything they (even just existing in the video). Their partner uses these perceived flaws to make them the scapegoat for all the relationship's problems.  Unfortunately, they want so desperately for the relationship to continue that they are willing to accept all blame no matter what. Even though this role of being the active "bad guy" or "the only heartbreaker" hurts them deeply (the water main burst and flooding) while their partner is absolved of any and all wrongdoings or atonement (by the window, only watching). They also accept that "for as long as [they're] together" this dynamic will never improve.  Thanks for coming to my TED talk

i genuinely do think it's just about how sometimes YOU are the problem and nobody else, in the relationship. i know people always want to shift blame, and to find a middle ground, to make things seem fair, but i truly think this is just about how at times, your relationship crumbles because of your mistakes. in the song she says that the partner can do nothing but watch her as she is destroying everything around her, and i know alot of people have said they think the other person in the relationship is maybe less caring than her, as she constantly tries... i actually don't think so. what else can you do than to grow tired from trying, when all the other person does is hurt you with their mistakes? what else can a person do when you're constantly dancing in your own fire (which i assume is her loneliness and misery, where she feels best), than to just watch, after having tried to fix the relationship? you can't blame the other person for growing tired of you running way and self destructing. in a way i see this as her, maybe not necessarily accepting, moreso aknowledging how much her own lack of healing has destroyed a relationship that could have had both sides completely involved. but it ends in you dancing in your own forest fire, over and over, until eventually the relationship ends, and your entire world dissapears. something you were so invested in, something you felt all these intense emotions for, doesn't exist. and you cease to exist, too.

I think in the part where she was dancing when the trees were burning towards the end was actually pretty symbolic. she was thrashing around like she was in pain and did hand movements upwards, like she was trying to regrow from the mess she made, or get out of the destruction she caused. at last, she finally gets away from the fire, only for the planet she was on to explode, which could symbolise her relationship with her partner. at the end, mitski is dressed in white, like a god or deity. she looked devastated, the planet meant a lot to her. it is thought that God created earth and the planets so it was like she was grieving over her own creation, which she also ended up destroying. since there was nothing left to destroy, she mourned over the emptiness of what once was a planet full of growth and life, which could symbolise a healthy relationship. she was aware of this self destruction, yet she couldn't do anything. another possible theory is that she knew she had to destroy it for the better, even though it could not be fixed, it would be better than watching it burn. and in the end, she not only destroyed the relationship, but herself.

one thing i absolutely love about mitski's music videos and performances is the way she moves and dances as she's singing.  the mix between traditional and then completely subverting it - the janky, kind of "wrongness" that ive heard some people call weird is just reflective of the songs she makes. these songs about the messy internal pain should not have to be presented by being 100% dramatically serious and conventional to exactly what the viewer would expect - the "strange" dancing conveys that inability to fit into what society expects of it all, and of womanhood in art i suppose.  i dont know if im just looking into this too much, but i have always loved this aspect of her work :)
